Steven Mangual, Common Justice — He came before the Board to introduce Common Justice, a program that’s an alternative to incarceration and mostly for the youth ages 16-26. It is the only program in the nation that works with violent felony offenders. The participants must first be approved by their crime victim. If they obtain a yes from their victim, they can be participants. If a no, then other services are available. It is a 15 months rigorous program. Upon graduation, the felony gets removed and changed to a misdemeanor. 3. Cory Shaw, NYC Parks — Programs & activities for all ages that are free or low cost. 4. Because of its long crossing distances, unprotected bike lanes and speeding encouraged by its wide roadway, this area impedes pedestrian safety. The committee also had a presentation requesting a Letter of Support for the design and construction of a new FDNY EMS headquarters at 1257 Morris Avenue between 167" & 169" Street. This new facility will replace the existing one at 1080 Ogden Avenue between 165" Street and 166™ Street. This new facility will be the restocking station for the ambulance supplies, it will be open 24 hours and it holds 11 units. It will provide 24 parking spots; therefore, they will not use any residential parking. The construction will take approximately two to three years to complete. At committee, it was voted unanimously to grant a Letter of Support. They will come back to committee at a later time with proposed renderings of the design and construction.
